rootpage-Air_travel_disruption_after_the_2010_Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull_eruption skin-vector action-view skin-vector-legacy"><div id="mw-page-base" class="noprint"></div>\n<div id="mw-head-base" class="noprint"></div>\n<div id="content" class="mw-body" role="main">\n\t<a id="top"></a>\n\t<div id="siteNotice" class="mw-body-content"><!-- CentralNotice --></div>\n\t<div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n\t</div>\n\t<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" >Air travel disruption after the 2010 Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull eruption</h1>\n\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\n\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t<div id="contentSub2"></div>\n\t\t\n\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\n\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull_volcanic_ash_composite.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull_volcanic_ash_composite.png/220px-Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull_volcanic_ash_composite.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull_volcanic_ash_composite.png/330px-Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull_volcanic_ash_composite.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull_volcanic_ash_composite.png/440px-Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull_volcanic_ash_composite.png 2x" data-file-width="726" data-file-height="726" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull_volcanic_ash_composite.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Composite map of the volcanic <a href="/wiki/Ash_cloud" class="mw-redirect" title="Ash cloud">ash cloud</a> (with <a href="/wiki/Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull" title="Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull">Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull</a> volcano in red) spanning 14\xe2\x80\x9325 April 2010, based on data by the London Volcanic Ash Advisory Centre\'s website<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Met_Office" title="Met Office">Met Office</a>, UK).</div></div></div>\n<p>In response to concerns that <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_ash" title="Volcanic ash">volcanic ash</a> ejected during the <a href="/wiki/2010_eruptions_of_Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull" title="2010 eruptions of Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull">2010 eruptions of Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull</a> in Iceland would damage <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_engine" title="Aircraft engine">aircraft engines</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Controlled_airspace" title="Controlled airspace">controlled airspace</a> of many European countries was closed to <a href="/wiki/Instrument_flight_rules" title="Instrument flight rules">instrument flight rules</a> traffic, resulting in what at the time was the largest air-traffic shut-down since World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-SMH2_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SMH2-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The closures caused millions of passengers to be stranded not only in Europe, but across the world. With large parts of European airspace closed to air traffic,<sup id="cite_ref-NASInfo_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NASInfo-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SFC15042010_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SFC15042010-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBCNews8622438_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCNews8622438-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> many more countries were affected as flights to, from, and over Europe were cancelled.\n</p><p>After an initial uninterrupted shutdown over much of northern Europe from 15 to 23 April, airspace was closed intermittently in different parts of Europe in the following weeks, as the path of the ash cloud was tracked. The <a href="/wiki/Ash_cloud" class="mw-redirect" title="Ash cloud">ash cloud</a> caused further disruptions to air travel operations in Scotland and Ireland on 4 and 5 May<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and in Spain, Portugal, northern Italy, Austria, and southern Germany on 9 May.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Irish and UK airspace closed again on 16 May and reopened on 17 May.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The eruption occurred beneath <a href="/wiki/Glacier" title="Glacier">glacial ice</a>. The cold water from the melting ice chilled the <a href="/wiki/Lava" title="Lava">lava</a> quickly, causing it to fragment into very small particles of glass (<a href="/wiki/Silica" class="mw-redirect" title="Silica">silica</a>) and ash, which were carried into the <a href="/wiki/Eruption_column" title="Eruption column">eruption plume</a>. The extremely fine ash particles and the large volume of steam from the glacial <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/meltwater" class="extiw" title="wikt:meltwater">meltwater</a> sent an ash plume <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_ash#Aircraft" title="Volcanic ash">hazardous to aircraft</a> rapidly high into the <a href="/wiki/Upper_atmosphere" title="Upper atmosphere">upper atmosphere</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian9032564_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian9032564-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The presence and location of the plume depended upon the state of the eruption and the winds. The large amount of glacial meltwater flowing into the eruption vent made this eruption so explosive that it ejected its ash plume directly into the <a href="/wiki/Jet_stream" title="Jet stream">jet stream</a>, which was unusually stable and south-easterly.<sup id="cite_ref-Newsweek16042010_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newsweek16042010-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The ash was then carried over Europe into some of the busiest airspace in the world.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association" title="International Air Transport Association">International Air Transport Association</a> (IATA) estimated that the airline industry worldwide would lose \xe2\x82\xac148 million (<span style="white-space: nowrap">US$200 million</span>, <span style="white-space: nowrap">GB\xc2\xa3130 million</span>) a day during the disruption.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> IATA stated that the total loss for the airline industry was around US$1.7 billion (\xc2\xa31.1 billion, \xe2\x82\xac1.3 billion).<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Airport_Operators_Association" title="Airport Operators Association">Airport Operators Association</a> (AOA) estimated that airports lost \xc2\xa380 million over the six-and-a-half days.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Over 95,000 flights had been cancelled all across Europe during the six-day airspace ban,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> with later figures suggesting 107,000 flights cancelled during an 8-day period, accounting for 48% of total air traffic and roughly 10 million passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Background"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Background</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Jet_engine_tolerance_to_airborne_particles"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Jet engine tolerance to airborne particles</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Airspace_restrictions_in_Europe"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Airspace restrictions in Europe</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4"><a href="#Disruptions_outside_Europe:_Canada"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Disruptions outside Europe: Canada</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a href="#Attempts_to_reopen_airspace"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Attempts to reopen airspace</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#Stranded_travellers"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Stranded travellers</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7"><a href="#Alternative_transport_routes"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Alternative transport routes</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href="#Criticism_of_airspace_closure"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Criticism of airspace closure</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9"><a href="#Military_flying"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Military flying</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10"><a href="#Impacts_of_the_disruption"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Impacts of the disruption</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Ash_cloud_maps"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Ash cloud maps</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_travel_disruption_after_the_2010_Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull_eruption&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Volcanic_Lavender.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Volcanic_Lavender.jpg/220px-Volcanic_Lavender.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Volcanic_Lavender.jpg/330px-Volcanic_Lavender.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Volcanic_Lavender.jpg/440px-Volcanic_Lavender.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="681" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Volcanic_Lavender.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dust particles suspended in the atmosphere scatter light from the setting sun, generating \'volcanic lavenders\' like this one over the flight path of <a href="/wiki/Leeds-Bradford_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Leeds-Bradford Airport">Leeds-Bradford Airport</a> in England during the aviation shutdown</div></div></div>\n<p>The London <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_Ash_Advisory_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Volcanic Ash Advisory Centre">Volcanic Ash Advisory Centre</a> (VAAC) was responsible for providing information about the <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_ash" title="Volcanic ash">ash plume</a> to the relevant <a href="/wiki/Civil_aviation_authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil aviation authority">civil aviation authorities</a> in the form of Volcanic Ash Advisories (VAA). On the basis of this, the authorities made decisions about when and where airspace should be closed due to the safety issues. Their decisions resulted in the cancellations of flights at airports across the world, not only in those countries where airspace was restricted. On 16 April 2010, 16,000 of Europe\'s usual 28,000 daily scheduled passenger flights were cancelled and on the following day 16,000 of the usual 22,000 flights were cancelled.<sup id="cite_ref-VoA17April_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VoA17April-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> By 21 April 95,000 flights had been cancelled.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Before this, the most severe restrictions to air travel in recent times were following the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">attacks of 11 September 2001 in the United States</a> when all civil air traffic (not just scheduled) in US airspace, and to and from the United States, was grounded for three days.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bill_McGuire_(volcanologist)" title="Bill McGuire (volcanologist)">Professor Bill McGuire</a> of the Aon Benfield UCL Hazard Research Centre said on 15 April that the most notable eruption of the <a href="/wiki/Volcanism_of_Iceland" title="Volcanism of Iceland">Icelandic volcano</a> <a href="/wiki/Laki" title="Laki">Laki</a> which occurred in 1783,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> would, if it occurred today "have the potential to severely affect air travel at high northern latitudes for six months or more". The last time the <a href="/wiki/Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull" title="Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull">Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull</a> <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcano</a> erupted, in 1821, it spewed ash for over a year.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Geophysicist" class="mw-redirect" title="Geophysicist">Geophysicists</a> in Iceland said that the production of ash from Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull was likely to continue at a comparable level for some days or even weeks; a geophysicist at the Icelandic Meteorological Office said, "Where it disrupts travel depends on the weather. It depends how the wind carries the <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_ash" title="Volcanic ash">ash</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Jet_engine_tolerance_to_airborne_particles">Jet engine tolerance to airborne particles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_travel_disruption_after_the_2010_Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull_eruption&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Jet engine tolerance to airborne particles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_ash_and_aviation_safety" title="Volcanic ash and aviation safety">Volcanic ash and aviation safety</a></div>\n<p>In 1982, <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_Flight_9" title="British Airways Flight 9">British Airways Flight 9</a> flew through volcanic ash of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Galunggung" class="mw-redirect" title="Mount Galunggung">Mount Galunggung</a>, <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a>, Indonesia, causing all 4 engines to shut down. However, the crew restarted all but one of the engines and <a href="/wiki/Emergency_landing" title="Emergency landing">landed safely</a>. Subsequently, there was an addition to the operations manuals, describing how to deal with volcanic ash.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Iceland\'s authorities had been warning the airlines for several years, asking them to determine the density of ash that is safe for their jet engines.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>But before the volcanic events of April 2010, aircraft engine manufacturers still had not defined specific particle levels above which engines were considered to be at risk.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_&#123;&#123;&#123;1&#125;&#125;&#125;"><a class="external autonumber" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Air_travel_disruption_after_the_2010_Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull_eruption#endnote_">[1]</a></sup> The general approach taken by airspace regulators was that if the ash concentration rose above zero, then the airspace was considered unsafe and was consequently closed.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The April eruption of Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull caused enough economic difficulties that aircraft manufacturers were forced to define specific limits on how much ash is considered acceptable for a jet engine to ingest without damage. On 21 April, the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil Aviation Authority">CAA</a> in conjunction with engine manufacturers, set new guidelines<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> which allowed aircraft to fly when there are levels of volcanic ash between 200 and 2000 micrograms (2 milligrams) of ash per cubic metre. These levels were declared by governments, aircraft manufacturers, and airlines not to have safety implications if appropriate maintenance and ash inspection procedures were followed.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From noon 18 May, the CAA further revised the safe limit upwards to 4 milligrams per cubic metre of air space.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Any airspace in which the ash density exceeds this limit is categorised as a <a href="/wiki/No_fly_zone" class="mw-redirect" title="No fly zone">no fly zone</a>.\n</p><p>To minimise the level of further disruption that this and other volcanic eruptions could cause, the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil Aviation Authority">CAA</a> announced the creation of a new category of restricted airspace called a <a href="/w/index.php?title=Time_Limited_Zone&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Time Limited Zone (page does not exist)">Time Limited Zone</a> (TLZ).<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Airspace categorised as TLZ is similar to airspace experiencing severe weather in that the restrictions are expected to be of a short duration; however, the key difference with TLZ airspace is that airlines must produce certificates of compliance in order for their aircraft to enter these areas. <a href="/wiki/Flybe" title="Flybe">Flybe</a> was the first airline to conform to these regulations and their aircraft will be permitted to enter airspace in which the ash density is between 2&#160;mg and 4&#160;mg per cubic metre.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airspace_restrictions_in_Europe">Airspace restrictions in Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_travel_disruption_after_the_2010_Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull_eruption&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Airspace restrictions in Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="infobox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin:0 0 1.5em 1.5em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-above" No data available for much of France and some other areas.</div></div></div>\n<p>Under international regulations, all scheduled passenger flights operate under the <a href="/wiki/Instrument_flight_rules" title="Instrument flight rules">instrument flight rules</a> (IFR) which requires clearance to be obtained from <a href="/wiki/Air_traffic_control" title="Air traffic control">air traffic control</a>. From 14 April onwards, the <a href="/wiki/Controlled_airspace" title="Controlled airspace">controlled airspace</a> was closed in several European countries and no IFR clearances were granted.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The airspace of Iceland itself was hardly disrupted in this period (although a change in the wind direction on 23 April caused the main airport to be closed).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>By 23 April, the restrictions were lifted over much of Europe through the introduction of new guidelines on volcanic ash density. After this date there were sporadic closures from time to time, notably in the UK, Ireland, and Iceland, but not a blanket shutdown.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td><b>Country</b></td>\n<td><b>Restrictions imposed</b>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/23px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/35px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/45px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a></td>\n<td>On 16 April, <a href="/wiki/Austro_Control" title="Austro Control">Austro Control</a> ceased air activities at airports in both <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Linz" title="Linz">Linz</a>; <a href="/wiki/Salzburg" title="Salzburg">Salzburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Innsbruck" title="Innsbruck">Innsbruck</a> stopped flights at 20:00 <a href="/wiki/Central_European_Summer_Time" title="Central European Summer Time">CEST</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Graz" title="Graz">Graz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Klagenfurt" title="Klagenfurt">Klagenfurt</a> followed at 23:00&#160;CEST. \xe2\x80\x93 35,500 feet (10,800&#160;m).\nThis means that aircraft on a route such as Tokyo to New York can fly over Denmark.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> As the ash cloud spread over Estonia on the night of 16 April, all flights were cancelled due to closure of airspace in <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Estonian airspace was partly opened in the evening of 19 April and completely late evening on 20 April.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Flag_of_Finland.svg/23px-Flag_of_Finland.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" title="Finland">Finland</a></td>\n<td>Finland closed its airspace at 00:00 <a href="/wiki/Eastern_European_Summer_Time" title="Eastern European Summer Time">EEST</a> on 16 April, having previously closed northern, western, and central parts of its airspace.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> On 19 April a gap formed in the ash cloud over Finland, and <a href="/wiki/Finavia" title="Finavia">Finavia</a> lifted flight restrictions at the airports of <a href="/wiki/Helsinki-Vantaa" class="mw-redirect" title="Helsinki-Vantaa">Helsinki-Vantaa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turku_Airport" title="Turku Airport">Turku</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tampere%E2%80%93Pirkkala_Airport" title="Tampere\xe2\x80\x93Pirkkala Airport">Tampere-Pirkkala</a> in the afternoon. During the five hours that Helsinki-Vantaa airport was open, there were a total of ten flights either arriving or departing.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> On 20 April the upper airspace was opened at 9,500 metres (31,200&#160;ft) altitude to international overflights above the occurrence of the ash.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> On 21 April, Helsinki-Vantaa Airport\'s air traffic control services are open and other airport services, like terminal services, are returning to normal by 12.00 noon. The airport was closed again at 3&#160;pm.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> On 22 April, Helsinki-Vantaa Airport was opened around 3&#160;pm, and was expected to remain open at least 24 hours.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" were closed.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> On 17 April, the <a href="/wiki/Direction_G%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale_de_l%27Aviation_Civile" class="mw-redirect" title="Direction G\xc3\xa9n\xc3\xa9rale de l&#39;Aviation Civile">Direction G\xc3\xa9n\xc3\xa9rale de l\'Aviation Civile</a> extended the suspension to 35 airports, including all Paris airports, until 08:00&#160;UTC+2 on Monday 19 April.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> On 18 April, the closure of the Paris airports was extended to at least 08:00&#160;UTC+2 on Tuesday 20 April.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img airspace was opened again for IFR and VFR at 11:00 CEST on 21 April.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/23px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" title="Hungary">Hungary</a></td>\n<td>Hungary\'s airspace was closed at 19:00 CEST on 16 April.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> It remained closed until 10:00&#160;UTC on Monday 19 April.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Flag_of_Ireland.svg/23px-Flag_of_Ireland.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Flag_of_Ireland.svg/46px-Flag_of_Ireland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a></td>\n<td>\n<p>On 15 April, the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Aviation_Authority" title="Irish Aviation Authority">Irish Aviation Authority</a> announced restrictions on flying in Irish airspace until <span class="nowrap">06:00 IST</span> on Friday 16 April at the earliest<sup id="cite_ref-rte15april2010_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rte15april2010-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Restrictions were lifted on flights to and from <a href="/wiki/Cork_(city)" title="Cork (city)">Cork</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Airport" title="Shannon Airport">Shannon</a>, and some regional airports by the day\'s end but restrictions remained at <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a> until <span class="nowrap">11:00 UTC+1</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-rte15april2010_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rte15april2010-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The government\'s emergency planning taskforce, which included several government departments, <a href="/wiki/Garda_S%C3%ADoch%C3%A1na" title="Garda S\xc3\xadoch\xc3\xa1na">An Garda S\xc3\xadoch\xc3\xa1na</a>, <a href="/wiki/Met_%C3%89ireann" title="Met \xc3\x89ireann">Met \xc3\x89ireann</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Aviation_Authority" title="Irish Aviation Authority">Irish Aviation Authority</a> (IAA), and Dublin Airport Authority (DAA), met on the evening of 15 April to discuss the emergency.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The taskforce had met at the National Emergency Co-ordinating Centre on five further occasions by the morning of 20 April 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 16 April, Irish air space was reopened for domestic flights from <span class="nowrap">10:00 IST</span> and westward transatlantic flights resumed from Dublin:<sup id="cite_ref-rte16april2010_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rte16april2010-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Irish flights which were scheduled to fly eastwards over the United Kingdom and continental European airspace remained grounded.<sup id="cite_ref-rte16april2010_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rte16april2010-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 17 April, the ash spread to most of Ireland, and all airspace was closed until 18:00&#160;UTC+01, and subsequently extended until 18:00 UTC+01 on Monday 19 April.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On Monday 19 April, the country\'s aviation chief warned that Dublin was "damned" and would be shut off to the rest of the world until Friday 23 April.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> On Tuesday 20 April, it was reported that at least 30,000 Irish people were still stranded abroad, unable to get home.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Those who were at home were opting for "staycations", as Irish holidaymakers swapped <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a> for <a href="/wiki/Ballybunion" title="Ballybunion">Ballybunion</a> in a boost for domestic tourism.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It had been anticipated that Irish air space would re-open for limited flights from 05:00 UTC+1 on 20 April; however, the volcanic ash cloud made this impossible. It was expected that normal flights will resume from Friday, 23 April, due to the backlog of flights.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Shannon Airport opened at 13:00 UTC+1 on 20 April (not for departing commercial flights) but Cork Airport and Dublin Airport remained closed.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 20 April at 21:00 UTC+1 Irish airspace fully re-opened, but air travellers were advised to contact their airline. It was expected that normal flights would resume on Friday 23 April.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> A statement from the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Aviation_Authority" title="Irish Aviation Authority">Irish Aviation Authority</a> said "[it] is expected that flights tomorrow [21 April] will focus on positioning aircraft and crews and full service by the airlines may take up to three days to recover. Passengers should consult airline websites before travelling to the airport for flights."<sup id="cite_ref-IrishResume_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IrishResume-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 4 May, Irish airspace closed from 07:00 to 13:00 IST. The IAA said the decision was based on information from the Volcanic Ash Advice Centre (VAAC). The no fly zone affected Dublin, Shannon, Galway, Sligo, Ireland West (Knock), Donegal, Cork, and Kerry.<sup id="cite_ref-IrishResume_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IrishResume-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> At 13:00 UTC+1 Irish airspace fully re-opened. However further closures and cancellations occurred the next day, on 5 May.\n<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span Airports throughout <a href="/wiki/Nord-Tr%C3%B8ndelag" title="Nord-Tr\xc3\xb8ndelag">Nord-Tr\xc3\xb8ndelag</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nordland" title="Nordland">Nordland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Troms" title="Troms">Troms</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Finnmark" title="Finnmark">Finnmark</a> were re-opened at times, as those areas were least affected by the ash: the largest of these, <a href="/wiki/Trondheim_Airport,_V%C3%A6rnes" title="Trondheim Airport, V\xc3\xa6rnes">Trondheim</a>, was opened for six hours on 16 April.\n<p>The total closure of Norwegian airspace included the 21 <a href="/wiki/Search_and_rescue" title="Search and rescue">search and rescue</a> and medical aircraft and helicopters in the country. The health authorities stated that the challenges faced were unprecedented in modern history, and ambulances and medical personnel were moved north and out of cities to decentralise the service and replace the lost aerial transport.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The air space caused most of the <a href="/wiki/Oil_platform" title="Oil platform">oil platforms</a> in the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> to not be able to fly in new personnel, causing existing crews to have to work until 18 April.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_Poland.svg/23px-Flag_of_Poland.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_Poland.svg/35px-Flag_of_Poland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_Poland.svg/46px-Flag_of_Poland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="800" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a></td>\n<td>Poland closed the northern part of its airspace at 18:00 UTC on 15 April. On 16 April its whole airspace was shut down.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n<p>The disruption affected the <a href="/wiki/Death_and_state_funeral_of_Lech_Kaczy%C5%84ski_and_Maria_Kaczy%C5%84ska" class="mw-redirect" title="Death and state funeral of Lech Kaczy\xc5\x84ski and Maria Kaczy\xc5\x84ska">funeral</a> for the Polish president <a href="/wiki/Lech_Kaczy%C5%84ski" title="Lech Kaczy\xc5\x84ski">Lech Kaczy\xc5\x84ski</a>, his wife <a href="/wiki/Maria_Kaczy%C5%84ska" title="Maria Kaczy\xc5\x84ska">Maria</a>, and the other victims who died in an <a href="/wiki/2010_Polish_Air_Force_Tu-154_crash" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 Polish Air Force Tu-154 crash">air crash</a> earlier in April. Family members decided not to postpone the ceremony, resulting in other countries\' dignitaries being unable to attend.\n</p>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Portugal.svg/23px-Flag_of_Portugal.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" 20 April that the cloud of volcanic ash entered the Portuguese airspace controlled by the Azorean island of Santa Maria, in an area still far from the national territory, and that the affected area was "very small".<sup id="cite_ref-google1_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-google1-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> For the most part, only flights to countries with closed airspaces were cancelled forcing numerous members of the government (including the president) who were away to return to the country by car from the UK, Austria, and Belgium.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> however several flights to the U.S. and elsewhere were also cancelled because of the unavailability of planes coming from other parts of Europe or carriers that required the planes to stop in their countries, such as Germany or France.<sup id="cite_ref-google1_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt=""
