srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Flag_of_Serbia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Serbia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Flag_of_Serbia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Serbia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="945" data-file-height="630" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a><br /><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Flag_of_Montenegro.svg/23px-Flag_of_Montenegro.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Flag_of_Montenegro.svg/35px-Flag_of_Montenegro.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Flag_of_Montenegro.svg/46px-Flag_of_Montenegro.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="320" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a><br /><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Flag_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.svg/23px-Flag_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Flag_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.svg/35px-Flag_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Flag_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.svg/46px-Flag_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="400" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a></td>\n<td>Air Traffic Services Agency of Serbia and Montenegro, shut down all traffic over <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>, Montenegro, part of international waters of the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic Sea</a>, and the upper airspace of <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> that it controls, at 14:00 UTC, 17 April.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The airspace was reopened at 22:00 UTC, 18 April.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Flag_of_Slovakia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Slovakia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Flag_of_Slovakia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Slovakia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Flag_of_Slovakia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Slovakia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="341" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a></td>\n<td>Slovakia\'s airspace was closed at 15:00 UTC on 16 April.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Flag_of_Slovenia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Slovenia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Flag_of_Slovenia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Slovenia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Flag_of_Slovenia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Slovenia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a></td>\n<td>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Transport_Ministry_of_Slovenia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Transport Ministry of Slovenia (page does not exist)">Transport Ministry</a> closed the airspace to the north of the <a href="/wiki/46th_parallel_north" title="46th parallel north">46th parallel</a> up to 35,500 feet (10,800&#160;m) at 22:00&#160;UTC on 16 April, and over the entire country at 06:00&#160;UTC on 17 April. The closure lasted until 19:10&#160;UTC on 18 April.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> It was the first closure of Slovenian airspace since the <a href="/wiki/Ten-Day_War" title="Ten-Day War">Ten-Day War</a> in 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> On 03:00&#160;UTC on 20 April, the airspace was closed again up to 20,500&#160;ft (6,200&#160;m).<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> On 07:00&#160;UTC on 21 April, the airspace was opened again without restrictions.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/23px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/35px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/45px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="500" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Aena" class="mw-redirect" title="Aena">Aena</a> closed seven airports in northern Spain at 20:00&#160;UTC+1 on 17 April: they were planned to remain closed until 10:00 on 18 April,<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> but one hour later, at 21:00 UTC+1 they started to operate again. At 08:30&#160;UTC+1 on 18&#160;11 April northern airports were closed, including <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, the country\'s second largest. At 12:00&#160;UTC+1 two more airports in the <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a> were closed, including Spain\'s third largest <a href="/wiki/Palma_de_Mallorca" title="Palma de Mallorca">Palma de Mallorca</a>. All 13 airports were expected to reopen at 20:00&#160;UTC+1 on 18 April. Other minor airports, not controlled by Aena, were closed as well, although it was thought they could be re-opened at 15:30&#160;UTC+1.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/23px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/35px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/46px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1000" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a></td>\n<td>Sweden\'s airspace was closed at 20:00 UTC on 15 April. Airspace north of <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6derhamn" title="S\xc3\xb6derhamn">S\xc3\xb6derhamn</a> was reopened at 16:45 CEST on 18 April.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Switzerland.svg/16px-Flag_of_Switzerland.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Switzerland.svg/24px-Flag_of_Switzerland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Switzerland.svg/32px-Flag_of_Switzerland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="512" />&#160;&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a></td>\n<td>The Federal Office of Civil Aviation issued a <a href="/wiki/NOTAM" title="NOTAM">notice to airmen</a> at 14:15&#160;UTC on 16 April stating that the FIR Switzerland<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2010)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> would be closed for <a href="/wiki/Visual_flight_rules" title="Visual flight rules">visual</a> and <a href="/wiki/Instrument_flight_rules" title="Instrument flight rules">instrument</a> flight rules operations from 21:59&#160;UTC on 16 April to 12:00&#160;UTC on 19 April.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Police, Search and Rescue (SAR) and emergency medical helicopter flights were exempted.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Swiss_International_Air_Lines" title="Swiss International Air Lines">Swiss International Air Lines</a> informed its customers on 16 April that the airports at <a href="/wiki/Zurich" class="mw-redirect" title="Zurich">Zurich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basel" title="Basel">Basel</a>, Geneva, and <a href="/wiki/Lugano" title="Lugano">Lugano</a> airports would be closed, and that all flights going to those airports would be cancelled.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/23px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/35px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/45px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a></td>\n<td>The Directorate General of Civil Aviation closed central-northern national air zones by 13:30 UTC (16:30 UTC+3) on 18 April between flight levels FL200 and FL350 until 09:00 UTC (12:00 UTC+3) on 19 April. All airports, however, remained open.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Flag_of_Ukraine.svg/23px-Flag_of_Ukraine.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Flag_of_Ukraine.svg/35px-Flag_of_Ukraine.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Flag_of_Ukraine.svg/45px-Flag_of_Ukraine.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a></td>\n<td>The Ministry of Transport closed most national air zones by 00:00 UTC+3 on 17 April: only southern airports remained open. Aircraft from <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, bound for <a href="/wiki/Kiev" class="mw-redirect" title="Kiev">Kiev</a>, landed at <a href="/wiki/Simferopol" title="Simferopol">Simferopol</a>. All Ukrainian airspace was closed by 15:00&#160;EEST on 17 April.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> was the third region in Europe, after Iceland and Norway, to be affected, with all Scottish airports being closed to <a href="/wiki/Instrument_flight_rules" title="Instrument flight rules">instrument flight rules (IFR)</a> operations by 04:00&#160;BST on 15 April. The United Kingdom\'s controlled airspace was closed to IFR flights at 11:00&#160;UTC (12:00&#160;<a href="/wiki/British_Summer_Time" title="British Summer Time">BST</a>) on 15 April.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> However, several Icelandair planes flying from Keflavik landed at Glasgow on 16 April.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> The last commercial flight to leave British airspace before the lockdown was imposed was a <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a> flight (number SQ317) from <a href="/wiki/London_Heathrow" class="mw-redirect" title="London Heathrow">London Heathrow</a> airport to <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Changi" class="mw-redirect" title="Singapore Changi">Singapore Changi</a> airport. It was officially scheduled to leave at 11:55&#160;BST but became airborne at 11:32.\n<p>There was no restriction on <a href="/wiki/Visual_flight_rules" title="Visual flight rules">visual flight rules</a> traffic. <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> <a href="/wiki/RAF_Search_and_Rescue_Force" title="RAF Search and Rescue Force">search and rescue aircraft</a> continued to operate as normal, as did flights between <a href="/wiki/Land%27s_End_Airport" title="Land&#39;s End Airport">Land\'s End</a> and the <a href="/wiki/St_Mary%27s_Airport_(Isles_of_Scilly)" class="mw-redirect" title="St Mary&#39;s Airport (Isles of Scilly)">Isles of Scilly</a> which operate in <a href="/wiki/Uncontrolled_airspace" title="Uncontrolled airspace">uncontrolled airspace</a> at an <a href="/wiki/Altitude#Altitude_in_aviation" title="Altitude">altitude</a> less than 3,000 feet (910&#160;m).<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There remained no commercial airliners in British airspace until the morning of 16 April, when an <a href="/wiki/Air_Transat" title="Air Transat">Air Transat</a> flight was given clearance to leave <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a> for Toronto.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On the evening of 20 April, it was announced that all the UK\'s airports would be opened from 22:00&#160;BST.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 4 May, the airspace over Northern Ireland and the west of Scotland closed from 07:00 to 13:00 UTC+1. The CAA said the decision was based on information from the Volcanic Ash Advice Centre (VAAC). The no fly zone affected both Belfast airports and Derry airport.\n<sup id="cite_ref-IrishResume_69-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IrishResume-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> At 13:00 UTC+1 the airspace over Northern Ireland and Scotland fully re-opened. However, further closures occurred on 5 May.\n<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 16 May, the airspace closed over much of the UK from 13:00 until 17 May 07:00 UTC+1. The airports affected were East Midlands, Manchester, Liverpool, Doncaster Sheffield, Humberside, Carlisle, Belfast City, Belfast International, Glasgow Prestwick, those on Scottish islands, and the Isle of Man. London airports remained open most of that period except for a period during the early morning of 17 May.\n<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Disruptions_outside_Europe:_Canada">Disruptions outside Europe: Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_travel_disruption_after_the_2010_Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull_eruption&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Disruptions outside Europe: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Almost every country with an international airport experienced some disruption due to flights to or from Europe being cancelled. Canada was the only country outside Europe recorded as having cancelled any flights due a risk from ash clouds in its own airspace.\n</p><p>The Canadian airspace was never closed or restricted because of volcanic ash. Although the UK Met Office map of 21 April<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> shows the ash cloud reaching <a href="/wiki/Labrador" title="Labrador">Labrador</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Maritimes" class="mw-redirect" title="Canadian Maritimes">Maritime provinces</a>, far eastern <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_St._Lawrence" class="mw-redirect" title="Gulf of St. Lawrence">Gulf of St. Lawrence</a>, concentrations were expected to be sparse.<sup id="cite_ref-Canada_ash_risk_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canada_ash_risk-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On Monday, 19 April, the combination of heavy fog with a warning by <a href="/wiki/Transport_Canada" title="Transport Canada">Transport Canada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nav_Canada" title="Nav Canada">Nav Canada</a> of a 30% risk of volcanic ash reaching <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s,_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="St. John&#39;s, Newfoundland and Labrador">St. John\'s</a> led to the cancellation of several flights scheduled to leave <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s_International_Airport" title="St. John&#39;s International Airport">St. John\'s International Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gander_International_Airport" title="Gander International Airport">Gander</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Deer_Lake_Regional_Airport" title="Deer Lake Regional Airport">Deer Lake</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Because of the heavy fog, it is unclear if the ash cloud warning was really the cause of the cancellations and delays in <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a>, and most flights returned to their normal schedule within the day.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Air_Canada" title="Air Canada">Air Canada</a> said their flights were "subject to some delays due to inclement weather, unrelated to ash cloud."<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> On Tuesday, 20 April, two <a href="/wiki/Air_Canada_Jazz" class="mw-redirect" title="Air Canada Jazz">Air Canada Jazz</a> flights between the <a href="/wiki/Magdalen_Islands" title="Magdalen Islands">Magdalen Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quebec_City" title="Quebec City">Quebec City</a> cancelled stop-offs in <a href="/wiki/Gasp%C3%A9,_Quebec" title="Gasp\xc3\xa9, Quebec">Gasp\xc3\xa9</a> because of ash over the <a href="/wiki/Michel-Pouliot_Gasp%C3%A9_Airport" title="Michel-Pouliot Gasp\xc3\xa9 Airport">Michel-Pouliot Gasp\xc3\xa9 Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Attempts_to_reopen_airspace">Attempts to reopen airspace</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_travel_disruption_after_the_2010_Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull_eruption&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Attempts to reopen airspace">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ash_plume_from_Eyjafjallajokull_Volcano_over_the_North_Atlantic,_15_April_2010,_annotated.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Ash_plume_from_Eyjafjallajokull_Volcano_over_the_North_Atlantic%2C_15_April_2010%2C_annotated.jpg/300px-Ash_plume_from_Eyjafjallajokull_Volcano_over_the_North_Atlantic%2C_15_April_2010%2C_annotated.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Ash_plume_from_Eyjafjallajokull_Volcano_over_the_North_Atlantic%2C_15_April_2010%2C_annotated.jpg/450px-Ash_plume_from_Eyjafjallajokull_Volcano_over_the_North_Atlantic%2C_15_April_2010%2C_annotated.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Ash_plume_from_Eyjafjallajokull_Volcano_over_the_North_Atlantic%2C_15_April_2010%2C_annotated.jpg/600px-Ash_plume_from_Eyjafjallajokull_Volcano_over_the_North_Atlantic%2C_15_April_2010%2C_annotated.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="360" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ash_plume_from_Eyjafjallajokull_Volcano_over_the_North_Atlantic,_15_April_2010,_annotated.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ash plume blowing across the North Atlantic on 15 April.</div></div></div>\n<p>Most airspace started to close from 15 April. However, in the days following there were brief windows free of the cloud at different locations which were exploited to make a few aircraft movements. There then followed test flights and pressure grew to re-evaluate the criteria for safe levels of ash to fly through.\n</p><p>On 16 April a 30-minute break at <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> allowed two flights to land, and one aircraft to be moved to Florida, empty (as there was no time for passengers to board). At <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Air_Transat" title="Air Transat">Air Transat</a> flight to Toronto took off while a <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a> flight from New York, and a <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cook_Group" title="Thomas Cook Group">Thomas Cook</a> flight from <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">Orlando</a><sup id="cite_ref-grauniad17_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grauniad17-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Icelandair" title="Icelandair">Icelandair</a> flights from <a href="/wiki/Keflavik" class="mw-redirect" title="Keflavik">Keflavik</a><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> landed.\n</p><p>On 17 April 2010, the president of German airline <a href="/wiki/Air_Berlin" title="Air Berlin">Air Berlin</a>, in an interview with the newspaper <a href="/wiki/Bild" title="Bild">Bild am Sonntag</a>, stated that the risks for flights due to this volcanic haze were nonexistent, because the assessment was based only on a computer simulation produced by the <a href="/wiki/VAAC" class="mw-redirect" title="VAAC">VAAC</a>. He went on to claim that the <a href="/wiki/Luftfahrt-Bundesamt" title="Luftfahrt-Bundesamt">Luftfahrt-Bundesamt</a> closed German airspace without checking the accuracy of these simulations.<sup id="cite_ref-bild01_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bild01-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Spokesmen for <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a> and <a href="/wiki/KLM" title="KLM">KLM</a> stated that during their test flights, required by the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, there were no problems with the aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-agi02_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agi02-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> On the morning of 17 April <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a> moved 10 aircraft from <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a> to <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> at low altitude following visual flight rules. There were no problems reported and no sign of damage to the planes.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> The same day, an Airbus belonging to <a href="/wiki/Ural_Airlines" title="Ural Airlines">Ural Airlines</a> attempted flying below the ash clouds from Moscow to <a href="/wiki/Rimini" title="Rimini">Rimini</a>. When the airplane was in Austrian airspace, the crew reported being low on fuel and diverted to <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, where the airplane landed safely.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On the morning of 18 April KLM successfully carried out a test flight from <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> to <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="D\xc3\xbcsseldorf">D\xc3\xbcsseldorf</a> with no problems. Afterwards, seven KLM planes with no passengers returned from D\xc3\xbcsseldorf to Amsterdam.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a> also performed a test flight from Paris to <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> In the evening of 18 April German airspace was partially re-opened for a period of 3 hours allowing a plane of stranded holidaymakers from <a href="/wiki/Faro,_Portugal" title="Faro, Portugal">Faro</a>, Portugal to land at <a href="/wiki/Hanover" title="Hanover">Hanover</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The vice president of the Dutch pilots union said "We are asking the authorities to really have a good look at the situation, because 100 per cent safety does not exist," Mr. Verhagen continued. "It\'s easy to close down air space because then it\'s perfectly safe, but at some time you have to resume flights."<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the afternoon of 19 April, German carriers Lufthansa and Air Berlin obtained permission for some flights from and to German airports under <a href="/wiki/Visual_Flight_Rules" class="mw-redirect" title="Visual Flight Rules">Visual Flight Rules</a>. Lufthansa started sending planes to long-haul destination in order to return stranded passengers later that day.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Late on 19 April and early on 20 April, some flights were permitted to take off in northern Europe, including from <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> and northern England, but <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester Airport</a>, that had planned to open on 20 April, remained closed because of a new ash cloud.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil Aviation Authority">Civil Aviation Authority</a> announced that all UK airports would be permitted to open from 2200 on 20 April. Twenty-six British Airways long-haul flights were already in the air and requesting permission to land.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By 20\xe2\x80\x9321 April several airlines confirmed that "air service will be resumed in stages" and started publishing lists of selected flights that were "most likely to be operated" within one single day.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> "Effective Thursday, 22 April, Lufthansa will resume normal flight operations and offer you the usual reliability", claimed the airline at 15:30 on 21 April.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stranded_travellers">Stranded travellers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_travel_disruption_after_the_2010_Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull_eruption&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Stranded travellers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The closure of the airspace left five million travellers stranded around the world,<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> of which up to a million were British according to <a href="/wiki/Association_of_British_Travel_Agents" class="mw-redirect" title="Association of British Travel Agents">ABTA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> Several thousand passengers were stranded in Asia,<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> the United States, and Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-QANTAS_cancels_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QANTAS_cancels-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Disruption was greater than that after the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">11 September attacks</a>, for example:<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>The disruption had a significant effect on schools across the United Kingdom because it came at the end of the Easter Holidays and many pupils and teachers were among those stranded abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Swedish and Norwegian charter tourists visiting Mallorca, Canary Islands, Cyprus, or Egypt were flown to Barcelona or Athens and then driven back to Sweden and Norway by bus<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> (a total distance of \xe2\x89\x883,400 kilometres (2,100&#160;mi) from Athens to Oslo by road taking two and a half days without a break).<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Around 600 Mexican middle-school students, ranging from 12 to 16 years old, who had attended a competition in England for foreign students and scheduled to return home on 18 April were stranded for almost a week. Some started to return to Mexico on 21 April and by 24 April most of them were already home.</li></ul>\n<p>Stranded passengers were not necessarily given priority over new passengers for return flights. <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a> told passengers in India and China that any free seats were being sold on the open market, and advised them to buy new tickets and seek reimbursement on return.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In addition to being stranded, some travelers also encountered issues with their visas after arriving at destinations unexpectedly:\n</p>\n<ul><li>At <a href="/wiki/Brussels_airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Brussels airport">Brussels airport</a>, 200 travelers from <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a> were unable to leave the building without a <a href="/wiki/Visa_(document)" class="mw-redirect" title="Visa (document)">visa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Passengers from <a href="/wiki/Kolkata" title="Kolkata">Kolkata</a> headed for London on an <a href="/wiki/Air_India" title="Air India">Air India</a> flight were diverted to <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>, where they were unable to leave the airport to seek accommodation because they did not have visas for Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>A group of passengers from the United Kingdom were facing arrest in <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a> over a breach of immigration laws, because they left the airport without visas.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>On 17 April the <a href="/wiki/UK_Border_Agency" title="UK Border Agency">UK Border Agency</a> announced that it would make allowances for travellers who were unable to leave the UK and whose visas had expired, provided that evidence of travel reservations during the travel disruption was presented.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a>, Serbia, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> also eased visa formalities for affected passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternative_transport_routes">Alternative transport routes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_travel_disruption_after_the_2010_Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull_eruption&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Alternative transport routes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Volcano_causes_queue_at_Bergen_Station.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Volcano_causes_queue_at_Bergen_Station.jpg/220px-Volcano_causes_queue_at_Bergen_Station.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Volcano_causes_queue_at_Bergen_Station.jpg/330px-Volcano_causes_queue_at_Bergen_Station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Volcano_causes_queue_at_Bergen_Station.jpg/440px-Volcano_causes_queue_at_Bergen_Station.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Volcano_causes_queue_at_Bergen_Station.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Queue at <a href="/wiki/Bergen_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Bergen Station">Bergen Station</a> as travelers wait to purchase train tickets from the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_State_Railways" class="mw-redirect" title="Norwegian State Railways">Norwegian State Railways</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Passengers destined for countries where airspace was closed had to switch to other modes of transport, possibly via airports still open in <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> to the east. Once inside Europe, many people tried to reach their final destination by train or road. People hired coaches, hire cars, and taxis while the train companies reported a large increase in passenger numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Eurostar" title="Eurostar">Eurostar</a> passenger trains were solidly booked, the <a href="/wiki/Eurotunnel" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurotunnel">Eurotunnel</a> car-carrying trains which run through the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel" title="Channel Tunnel">Channel Tunnel</a> were very busy, and additional services were scheduled. Travel conditions in France were compounded by an ongoing rail strike affecting long-distance trains.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Most UK and Irish ferry routes were exceptionally busy and coach operator <a href="/wiki/Bus_%C3%89ireann" title="Bus \xc3\x89ireann">Bus \xc3\x89ireann</a> arranged extra <a href="/wiki/Eurolines" title="Eurolines">Eurolines</a> services between Ireland and England via ferry.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The websites Twitter and Facebook, as well as other sites like Roadsharing, were used to arrange alternative travel plans involving boats and ships, trains, and other forms of transportation such as cars, as well as to try to find rooms for the night in the cities where they were stuck.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> As an alternative to face-to-face business meetings, <a href="/wiki/Videoconferencing" class="mw-redirect" title="Videoconferencing">videoconferencing</a> was also used by the European Union, governments, and companies.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Many people who had to travel, particularly those stranded while away from their home countries, faced large costs for unanticipated travel and accommodation at a time of scarcity.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Some costs were covered by compensation from airlines and travel insurance,<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> although there were many disputes over payments.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Some people incurred large <a href="/wiki/Taxicab" title="Taxicab">taxicab</a> fares over long distances, such as English actor <a href="/wiki/John_Cleese" title="John Cleese">John Cleese</a>, who took a taxi from <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a> to <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> and paid \xe2\x82\xac3,000 for the journey.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 18 April 2010, <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Government of the United Kingdom">UK Government ministers</a> announced a plan for flights to land and take off in Spain, and to transport passengers by sea back to the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> On 19 April, the cabinet crisis response committee (<a href="/wiki/Cabinet_Office_Briefing_Room" class="mw-redirect" title="Cabinet Office Briefing Room">COBRA</a>) decided that <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> ships should be utilised to <a href="/wiki/Repatriation" title="Repatriation">repatriate</a> stranded British travellers, in <a href="/wiki/Operation_Cunningham" title="Operation Cunningham">Operation Cunningham</a>. <a href="/wiki/HMS_Ark_Royal_(R07)" title="HMS Ark Royal (R07)">HMS <i>Ark Royal</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/HMS_Ocean_(L12)" title="HMS Ocean (L12)">HMS <i>Ocean</i></a>, and <a href="/wiki/HMS_Albion_(L14)" title="HMS Albion (L14)">HMS <i>Albion</i></a> were deployed, but only Albion was directly involved in repatriation.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the disruption in <a href="/wiki/Transatlantic_flight" title="Transatlantic flight">transatlantic flight</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cunard_Line" title="Cunard Line">Cunard Line</a> said its volume of calls inquiring about booking passage on its <a href="/wiki/Ocean_liner" title="Ocean liner">ocean liner</a> <a href="/wiki/RMS_Queen_Mary_2" class="mw-redirect" title="RMS Queen Mary 2">RMS <i>Queen Mary 2</i></a> by stranded air passengers wishing to <a href="/wiki/Transatlantic_crossing" title="Transatlantic crossing">cross by ship</a> had tripled since the weekend of 16 April.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_of_airspace_closure">Criticism of airspace closure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_travel_disruption_after_the_2010_Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull_eruption&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Criticism of airspace closure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>There was much criticism by airlines, which suffered large financial losses, of the airspace closures as unnecessary; however, the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_the_Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Presidency of the Council of the European Union">EU transport presidency</a> disagreed, saying that "This situation is causing them important losses, but safety is paramount".<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_flying">Military flying</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_travel_disruption_after_the_2010_Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull_eruption&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Military flying">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Some military aircraft which flew during the period of closure suffered engine damage, although no crashes were reported.\n</p><p>On 15 April, five <a href="/wiki/Finnish_Air_Force" title="Finnish Air Force">Finnish Air Force</a> <a href="/wiki/F-18" class="mw-redirect" title="F-18">F-18</a> fighter jets on exercise flew into the ash cloud in northern Finland. Volcanic dust was found on the engines of three of the aircraft and a further inspection revealed extensive damage by molten glass deposits inside the combustion chamber of one of the engines. The engines were sent for disassembly and overhaul. As a result, all unnecessary military flights were cancelled except for identification flights to enforce sovereign airspace. Meanwhile, a <a href="/wiki/BAE_Hawk" class="mw-redirect" title="BAE Hawk">BAE Hawk</a> trainer with special equipment to sample the volcanic dust was being flown from the 41st squadron in <a href="/wiki/Kauhava" title="Kauhava">Kauhava</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> Even short test flights with an F-18 revealed engine damage sufficient to destroy engines.<sup id="cite_ref-GlassBuild_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GlassBuild-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 19 April, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> reported finding molten glass in the engines of at least one <a href="/wiki/F-16" class="mw-redirect" title="F-16">F-16</a>, the result of flying through the ash cloud, leading to the scaling-down of U.S. military exercises.<sup id="cite_ref-GlassBuild_169-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GlassBuild-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> flights to <a href="/wiki/Selly_Oak_Hospital" title="Selly Oak Hospital">Selly Oak Hospital</a> in Birmingham were grounded, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Ministry_of_Defence" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Ministry of Defence">United Kingdom Ministry of Defence</a> considered flying <a href="/wiki/British_Forces_casualties_in_Afghanistan_since_2001" title="British Forces casualties in Afghanistan since 2001">British casualties of the Afghan War</a> to <a href="/wiki/International_Security_Assistance_Force" title="International Security Assistance Force">coalition countries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian18Apr2010Impact_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian18Apr2010Impact-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 23 April it was announced that British <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> training flights had been suspended following volcanic ash damage to the engines of <a href="/wiki/Eurofighter_Typhoon" title="Eurofighter Typhoon">Eurofighter Typhoon</a> aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-grounded_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grounded-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Impacts_of_the_disruption">Impacts of the disruption</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_travel_disruption_after_the_2010_Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull_eruption&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Impacts of the disruption">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_the_April_2010_Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull_eruption" title="Effects of the April 2010 Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull eruption">Effects of the April 2010 Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull eruption</a></div>\n<p>The disruption accelerated the integration of the national air traffic control systems into the <a href="/wiki/Single_European_Sky" title="Single European Sky">Single European Sky</a> and the immediate creation of a crisis coordination group to handle future transportation disruptions.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The ash indirectly affected <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_the_April_2010_Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull_eruption#Cultural_impacts" title="Effects of the April 2010 Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull eruption">many scheduled cultural and sporting events</a> because key participants were unable to attend, including the funeral of Polish president <a href="/wiki/Lech_Kaczy%C5%84ski" title="Lech Kaczy\xc5\x84ski">Lech Kaczy\xc5\x84ski</a> in <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Krak\xc3\xb3w">Krak\xc3\xb3w</a> on 18 April 2010.  The funeral was to have been attended by 69&#160;presidents, prime ministers, and other heads of states.  Almost half of these, including <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Luis Rodr\xc3\xadguez Zapatero">Jos\xc3\xa9 Luis Rodr\xc3\xadguez Zapatero</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Harper" title="Stephen Harper">Stephen Harper</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Sarkozy" title="Nicolas Sarkozy">Nicolas Sarkozy</a>, were unable to travel to Poland because of the disrupted air traffic.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There was also a wider impact on the economies of several countries. However, there were some environmental advantages arising from a saving of around 1.3 to 2.8 million tonnes of carbon dioxide emissions.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ash_cloud_maps">Ash
